I thoroughly enjoyed his presentation and now follow his routine to the &#34;T&#34;. Dickey informs curly girls not to use foaming/sudsing shampoos as they are very drying and potentially damaging to the hair. As an amateur cosmetic chemist I certainly understood this and set out to find a &#34;ready-made&#34; product to test and possibly reproduce in the &#34;lab&#34;. Hair Rules' Cleansing Cream was too expensive (though I do plan on trying to dupe that product) for my blood and I wanted something I could use immediately.<br /><br />I chose this product not only for the hype, but also because it has three surfactants...2 cationic and 1 non-ionic surfactants which are not great cleaners (they won't be able to dissolve large oil/grease particles) since their primary functions are &#34;conditioners&#34;, but they clean. The chlorides cetrimonium and stearalkonium both show antimicrobial activity, and cetrimonium has been shown to remove silicone. All the while, they're both FANTASTIC conditioners, softeners, and reduce combing forces! Cetrimonium is a wonderful detangling agent and stearalkonium is a great antistatic agent. Peg-40 Castor oil--the non ionic surfactant--is a multi-purpose ingredient.<br /><br />My experience with the product was promising. I'm a &#34;raker&#34;, meaning I just rake product through my hair and finger detangle as I go. I was able to very easily run this product through my hair after fully saturating my hair with water. It's runny enough to reach my scalp, but heavy enough to add weight to my curls and form a pattern. My hair felt clean after using this product...almost a little too clean which was a nice surprise. I wasn't expecting that clean feeling from a &#34;no suds&#34; shampoo. My hair didn't feel stripped, just clean. As an aside: I used this product before getting my hair done and my stylist even mentioned how clean my hair was. As I Am gets 4/5 stars from me. Only 4 stars because I don't like packaging...A jar? Really marketing people??
